  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bfba2fea-014b-4789-8b0a-6a62d09687d9'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText10703902415495075200" style="display:none">(Young Adult/original version)<br /><br />What if you knew when someone was going to die? For seventeen-year-old Ember, life is death. With a simple touch, she knows when someone will die. It’s her curse and the reason she secludes herself from the world. The only person who knows her secret is her best friend Raven. Then she meets Asher Morgan. He’s gorgeous, mysterious, and is the only person Ember can't sense death from. So when he pushes into her life, she doesn’t mind. But when unexplained deaths start to haunt her town, Ember starts questioning why she can’t sense Asher's death and what he may be hiding.</span>

      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

<div id="review_593121875" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/593121875" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17800114-ember">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=teen-young-adult">teen-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=you-call-this-a-book">you-call-this-a-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/722677-tess?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer593121875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12757641505941722357">wow. This book is Terrible.<br/>Hate the main character. Are all teens ADD now? Her life is too messed up to believe, she sees people's deaths, and yet she is mainly concerned with whether or not she should go on a date with either of the two new boys in her class. Oh, not to mention her car gets run off the road into a lake and she doesn't even seem to mind. Plus her best friend seems to be losing her mind recently, but yeah sure let's go to another party. or wait, let me write terrible poetry on my</span>
  <span id="freeText12757641505941722357" style="display:none">wow. This book is Terrible.<br />Hate the main character. Are all teens ADD now? Her life is too messed up to believe, she sees people's deaths, and yet she is mainly concerned with whether or not she should go on a date with either of the two new boys in her class. Oh, not to mention her car gets run off the road into a lake and she doesn't even seem to mind. Plus her best friend seems to be losing her mind recently, but yeah sure let's go to another party. or wait, let me write terrible poetry on my wall instead. How about I just read terrible poetry on my boyfriend's tattooed body?<br />The angel &amp; grim reaper great war and constant battle was confusing and scattered. Her best friend just happened to read something in a book that sounds remarkably like Ember's life, and then conveniently finds passages at all the right times...Because you don't see where that is headed at all. But wait, there's another party and dead teen to angst about, who has time to worry about angels and reapers?<br />Actually "scattered" pretty well sums up this paranormal nightmare. teens are missing or dead all over town, and nobody cares. The main girls flit from horror situation to school to parties and back to horror like it's supposed to make sense. all the while we are supposed to believe that in 12 years of seeing death Ember still hasn't figured out a way to either get used to it, or found a way to better avoid touching anyone. Gag.<br />and finally, the major inaccuracies with ravens seriously irritated me. if you are going to have black feather shedding omens of death on every page, at least get their characteristics right.<br />Just... Don't read it. I found nothing redeeming in this story, which hasn't happened to me in a long time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12757641505941722357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Ashleyjo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33970054-ashleyjo"><img alt="Ashleyjo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466919724p2/33970054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1688374139?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleyjo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleyjo" href="/user/show/33970054-ashleyjo">Ashleyjo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781484020166" href="/book/show/17727238-ember-x">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1688374139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8048581168858767958">I promise that I'm not being dramatic or trying to be mean, but this is what I imagine <i>would </i> happen <i>if </i> an author were to trip on a shit ton of pharmaceutical substances while watching something like... <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467698223i/19618737.jpg' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>That said, I did keep reading. While the plot twists are glaringly obvious, there's still this WTF element to it that's hard to look away from. <br/><br/><b>What's What </b> <br/><br/>The blurb doesn't really tell you what you're getting here. <br/><br/>Girl sees people's deaths through touch. It's a burden, a curse. She has one fr</span>
  <span id="freeText8048581168858767958" style="display:none">I promise that I'm not being dramatic or trying to be mean, but this is what I imagine <i>would </i> happen <i>if </i> an author were to trip on a shit ton of pharmaceutical substances while watching something like... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467698223i/19618737.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>That said, I did keep reading. While the plot twists are glaringly obvious, there's still this WTF element to it that's hard to look away from. <br><br><b>What's What </b> <br><br>The blurb doesn't really tell you what you're getting here. <br><br>Girl sees people's deaths through touch. It's a burden, a curse. She has one friend, who's a bitch. Enter two hot dudes different as *clears throat* day and night. While she favors one over the other and only has sex with one, this is still A TRIANGLE!! <br><br>What follows is 80% YA fluff - panty dropping swoon, dates, making out, parties. Some artsy shit &amp; poetry is thrown in. And the whole thing is sprinkled with mofos dying every five minutes minutes. <br><br>It's overwritten. <br><br>Subject shifts are jarring, but I'll say the author at least gives <i> that </i> a purpose by the end. <br><br>The last 20% is the best part of the book. All is pretty much expected, but the pacing speeds up and provides some action at least. <br><br>However, it does feel like we've circled the globe here just for the FMC to figure out what she should've known all along and end up in pretty much the same spot she starts the book. <br><br>And, there are a shit ton of plot questions that should've been answered here but aren't. <br><br>Mild Cliffhanger ending. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467697370ra/19618697.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b> Rewrite </b> <br><br>This book was rewritten from a YA novel. Yes, it includes some graphic sexual scenes, language, and murder. BUT, aside from the subject matter, this STILL READS LIKE YA. The dialogue, actions, and setting all have a juvenile tone. <br><br><br><b> Bottom Line </b> <br><br>Pacing is slow. <br><br>Lots of useless, fluffy info. <br><br>Not a fan of the author 's writing and storytelling style.<br><br>The frequency of the artsy, poetry prose became annoying. <br><br>I did like the premise and bones of the story. <br><br>The characters came across as YA high school kids, not 19 + year-olds. <br><br>The FMC's stupidity and disbelief over what she is and what the guys are is unbelievable. <br><br>Overall, 2 unimpressed stars:/</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_323065409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/323065409" />
    <a title="Michelle&#39;s Paranormal Vault of Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books"><img alt="Michelle&#39;s Paranormal Vault of Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373846671p2/8875051.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/323065409?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle&#39;s Paranormal Vault of Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle&#39;s Paranormal Vault of Books" href="/user/show/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books">Michelle&#39;s Paranormal Vault of Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books?shelf=owned-e-books">owned-e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8875051-michelle-s-paranormal-vault-of-books?shelf=angels">angels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer323065409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18327497020680851997">This review is also at my blog, with added pictures too <a href='http://concisebookreviewsbymichelle.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michelle's Paranormal Vault of Books</a><br/><br/>WOW, this book was amazing; Jessica has done it again, created a great story, which puts you on the edge of your seat! I stayed up half the night to finish this, I could not stop. I had to know what happened next. This book has a broken family, betrayal, impossible love triangle, (but not really in the way you think) and trying to guess who or what anyone is, is hard, you will be wrong!<br/><br/>In this book, Ember</span>
  <span id="freeText18327497020680851997" style="display:none">This review is also at my blog, with added pictures too <a href="http://concisebookreviewsbymichelle.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Michelle's Paranormal Vault of Books</a><br><br>WOW, this book was amazing; Jessica has done it again, created a great story, which puts you on the edge of your seat! I stayed up half the night to finish this, I could not stop. I had to know what happened next. This book has a broken family, betrayal, impossible love triangle, (but not really in the way you think) and trying to guess who or what anyone is, is hard, you will be wrong!<br><br>In this book, Ember is faced with death daily. Anyone she touches, she sees their death omen, and she sees how they are going to die. And some die young and brutally. She has had to face a broken family; her mother called her crazy, and sent her to live with her dad when she was 4 or so. Then had to get back with her mom when something happened with her dad. Basically, she lives with a mother who is out of it most days. Ember is a Goth girl, who is described with long silky black hair, and grey/light blue eyes, pale skin. I pictured her looking like Ksena Solo from Lost Girl on Sci Fi channel, (she plays Kenzi the human, goth girl)<a href="https://www.google.com/search?q=ksenia+solo&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;stick=H4sIAAAAAAAAAONgVuLSz9U3MDOtLDIzAgBBvalpDgAAAA&amp;prmd=imvnso&amp;tbm=isch&amp;tbo=u&amp;source=univ&amp;ei=yokmUJSXGJLiyAHjqYCAAg&amp;ved=0CGEQsAQ&amp;biw=1366&amp;bih=600" rel="nofollow noopener">Ksena Solo Photos Here</a><br><br>She is a very strong character, and she deals with things daily that I would cringe at if it was me. Not all is what it seems. We have 2 new boys come into the picture, and I love how we do not really know for sure, which is the bad evil one, and which is not. I do not want to say much to spoil anything, this will remain spoiler free. I will add a few good teasers for you.<br><br><i> “Open your eyes,” a deep voice asserts. “Come on, not yet. Open your eyes, God damn it.” The whisper alters to a desperate plea. “Please Ember… please wake up… you have to be one of them—I know you are.” </i><br><br>I didn’t feel like I liked Raven, her best friend a lot, I did some, but I do not trust her, and feel bad for Ember that she basically has no one to talk to. I really liked Asher, he has black hair and grey eyes, pale skin, very goodlooking, he is a sweet guy, and right away was drawn to him (I pictured him looking like a young <a href="http://www.imdb.com/name/nm1330560/mediaindex" rel="nofollow noopener">Garrett Hedlum</a>, like he looked in the Eragon movie, with the longer black hair, he was in Tron too, but with blond hair). Cameron, I also liked some, but didn’t trust him, he has blond hair, described as dark eyes, not sure color, may have been blue, but something about him seemed too perfect. (I pictured him as a young <a href="http://www.fanpop.com/spots/cam-gigandet/images/4125814/title/cam-gigandet-photo" rel="nofollow noopener">Cam Gigandet</a>, like he was in the movie Never Back Down, or Roommate movie, not like when James in Twilight) I feel all the characters were developed very nicely.<br><br>I was happy with the ending, it was left open, as I know it’s a series, but not on a huge cliffhanger to where you want to scream, we don’t have that, but it still does leave us wanting more, like it should.<br><br>Overall, Amazing story, I am honored I was able to read an ARC for Jessica. I highly recommend this book to any fan of Jessica, OR anyone who likes a great paranormal story. You won’t be disappointed!<br><br>I only have one negative thing to say, I don't like the book cover. The girl on cover looks nothing like the description, she has dark eyes and not even pretty, where Ember is describes as very pretty with the light grey/light blue eyes, and that combo with black hair is very attractive, like the the example I said above, she would look more like Ksolo than the cover. I am sure a computer generated girl with the proper look would be better, if the right model isn't found. Just my opinion. The cover actually turns me away, if I would not have known Jessica's work, and it was a book I just seen, I would have passed it up. I am guilty of the whole judging books by the covers. Sorry, but so many people are.<br><br>I was provided and ARC of this book for my honest review from the author.<br><br><b>Summary:</b><br><i>What if you knew when someone was going to die?<br><br>For seventeen-year-old Ember, life is death. With a simple touch, she knows when someone will die. It’s her curse and the reason she secludes herself from the world. The only person who knows her secret is her best friend Raven. <br><br>Then she meets Asher Morgan. He’s gorgeous, mysterious, and is the only person Ember can't sense death from. So when he pushes into her life, she doesn’t mind.<br><br>But when unexplained deaths start to haunt her town, Ember starts questioning why she can’t sense Asher's death and what he may be hiding.</i><br><br><a href="http://concisebookreviewsbymichelle.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="" width="300" height="100" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379783487i/445881._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

<div id="review_605490394" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605490394" />
    <a title="Jaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5686766-jaye"><img alt="Jaye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457065011p2/5686766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605490394?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaye" href="/user/show/5686766-jaye">Jaye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15924677-ember-x">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5686766-jaye?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5686766-jaye?shelf=erotica-adult-contemporary">erotica-adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5686766-jaye?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605490394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4129880205734642395">Couldn't finish this one. I thought it was badly written almost as if the author had rushed through it. It had a very overdone, melodramatic, and juvenile feel to it. Not something I was looking for.<br/><br/>A lot of the language and dialogue was extremely fanciful. Not to mention, it was all about the raven. Ravens abounded. They were everywhere. Not only as a reference to the actual bird, but as the name of Ember's friend; it was also used as a descriptor. There were a lot of raven feathers, too.<br/><br/>Moreov</span>
  <span id="freeText4129880205734642395" style="display:none">Couldn't finish this one. I thought it was badly written almost as if the author had rushed through it. It had a very overdone, melodramatic, and juvenile feel to it. Not something I was looking for.<br /><br />A lot of the language and dialogue was extremely fanciful. Not to mention, it was all about the raven. Ravens abounded. They were everywhere. Not only as a reference to the actual bird, but as the name of Ember's friend; it was also used as a descriptor. There were a lot of raven feathers, too.<br /><br />Moreover, there were aspects that bothered me. For example, the story makes it seem like ritualistic murder was an everyday thing. There wasn't any real lead up to this story arc. Also, Ember doesn't tell Raven how she will die--at least not in the portion I read. She justifies this by saying death is written in stone; nobody can change it. How did she arrive at this conclusion? Why not tell Raven she's supposed to die a horrible painful death? The reason she gives for not trying to stop this wasn't adequate for me.<br /><br />I don't know. I just didn't like it. The sex scenes weren't that good either. No real heat. Almost awkward. I expected more from this author.</span>

<div id="review_500430346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/500430346" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4039480-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423092907p2/4039480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/500430346?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/4039480-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4039480-amanda?shelf=young-adult-novels">young-adult-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4039480-amanda?shelf=did-not-like-it">did-not-like-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4039480-amanda?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer500430346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3354235987942714401">I see a lot of 3-5 star reviews for this book...and I'm confused. Did we all read the same book, here? <br/>This was awful. Shockingly bad. I hate to abandon any book so I forced myself to finish it. I'm surprised my eyes didn't bleed out of my skull. <br/>Everything felt ridiculously contrived and a lot of the supposed angst was just laughable. I love a depressing or 'angsty' read, but the image of a teenage girl wandering around a graveyard and spouting <u>really</u> bad poetry made me chuckle. And not in a go</span>
  <span id="freeText3354235987942714401" style="display:none">I see a lot of 3-5 star reviews for this book...and I'm confused. Did we all read the same book, here? <br />This was awful. Shockingly bad. I hate to abandon any book so I forced myself to finish it. I'm surprised my eyes didn't bleed out of my skull. <br />Everything felt ridiculously contrived and a lot of the supposed angst was just laughable. I love a depressing or 'angsty' read, but the image of a teenage girl wandering around a graveyard and spouting <u>really</u> bad poetry made me chuckle. And not in a good way. <br />The author's habit of making her say incredibly annoying things to get across how alone she feels just made me even more irritated. <br />The whole book is very bad, but here are some quotes from the first chapter: <br /><i> <br />My gaze travels upward to a statuesque carving of a hooded figure. Its head is tucked down and in its hand is a scythe.<br />“The Grim Reaper, huh?” I rise to my feet, stretching out my long legs, and tilt my head up. “I bet you know what it’s like, don’t you? To be surrounded by death all the time? I bet you understand me.”<br /><br /><br />A black raven swoops down from one of the trees and circles in front of me.<br />"Why are you always following me?” I whisper to the raven. “Is it because you know what I am—a symbol of death like you?”<br /></i><br />I really would not recommend this to anyone. Sorry. It's just not my cup of tea. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3354235987942714401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5650574609851517577">I found this on amazon for free and said "Hey! Another book by Jessica!" So I got it. <br/><br/>I really don't know what to say because I am just soooo mind blown. <br/><br/>I really liked Ember. Although there were a few times where I thought she could give Raven a piece of her mind. She's quiet, and sometimes her quietness got a little annoying. At certain parts of the book I was screaming at her to say something. She's way too nice for her own good, something I can relate to. <br/><br/>Raven was a little on the wild side.</span>
  <span id="freeText5650574609851517577" style="display:none">I found this on amazon for free and said "Hey! Another book by Jessica!" So I got it. <br /><br />I really don't know what to say because I am just soooo mind blown. <br /><br />I really liked Ember. Although there were a few times where I thought she could give Raven a piece of her mind. She's quiet, and sometimes her quietness got a little annoying. At certain parts of the book I was screaming at her to say something. She's way too nice for her own good, something I can relate to. <br /><br />Raven was a little on the wild side. She reminded me a lot of Vee from Hush, Hush. I liked her. She was bubbly and damn was she persistent. I did want to punch her a few times though. <br /><br />Asher. Mmm. Another name to add to the list. I was worried the whole time that he would turn out to be the bad guy. That's my luck. If he doesn't die, then he's the bad guy. This time, though he was the good guy and he lived. I'm jumping for joy, actually. <br /><br />Cameron. I hated this guy. I want him to die I hate him so much. He's too cocky and really annoying. He's too...territorial. Especially over things...or people, that don't belong to him. I wanted to punch him. <br /><br />This book was hard to put down because there were so many things that caught my attention. Like Raven's bitchy attitude towards Ember. And I just really really wanted to know what was up with the X on Raven's shoulder. And why Ember was seeing people hanging from trees one minute and then they'd just disappear. And mostly because I wanted to know why Ember could tell how someone would die. <br /><br />The only reason this book got 4 stars is because of the goddamn cliffhanger. But despite the cliffhanger, this was an amazing book and I'm recommending this to everyone. <br /><br />Enjoy! :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7967429410251640304">Actual rating 2.5 stars.<br/><br/>Blegh. Meh.<br/><br/>This was really, really average. Like, precisely average.<br/><br/>I remember liking Sorensen's earlier work, <i>The Fallen Star</i>. I thought it was entertaining albeit the writing sounded like a paranormal chick lit. <br/><br/>So, of course, a year later, I expected more from Sorensen. Much more. She wrote a bunch of other books in between <i>The Fallen Star</i> and <i>Ember.</i><br/><br/>*sigh*<br/><br/>Very well, it came to this anyway. I don't think I'll ever finish The Fallen Star series.<br/><br/>Ember. At first glance, it</span>
  <span id="freeText7967429410251640304" style="display:none">Actual rating 2.5 stars.<br><br>Blegh. Meh.<br><br>This was really, really average. Like, precisely average.<br><br>I remember liking Sorensen's earlier work, <i>The Fallen Star</i>. I thought it was entertaining albeit the writing sounded like a paranormal chick lit. <br><br>So, of course, a year later, I expected more from Sorensen. Much more. She wrote a bunch of other books in between <i>The Fallen Star</i> and <i>Ember.</i><br><br>*sigh*<br><br>Very well, it came to this anyway. I don't think I'll ever finish The Fallen Star series.<br><br>Ember. At first glance, it has a complete package. Gorgeous cover, interesting blurb, original mythology, reapers, Edgar Allan Poe,<br><br>death,<br><br>more EDGAR ALLAN POE,<br><br>more DEATH.<br><br>In short, this book has the potential to be the perfect gothic book for me but sadly, the execution was so average, it left me disappointed. So, so disappointed.<br><br>First, there's the duality of Ember and Raven. Contrary to the names, it's Ember who always wear black and it's Raven who has bubblegum pink hair. Anyway, I don't understand to why there's a need to create this unpopular, awkward or probably nerdy main female protagonist who is best friends with this popular, stylish girl. I believe there are more facades of high school teenagers than these stereotypes. <br><br>The male characters were really uninspiring. Sure, they do have interesting backgrounds but blegh, I don't get the romance at all. I find it really hormone-driven.<br><br>The plot is choppy. It was really hard to keep track of everything. Things just move from one scene to another in the next line.<br><br>To wrap it up, this was definitely a fast read but sadly, it failed to trigger even the tiniest bit of emotions out of me.<br><br>Oh well.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380381102ra/738251.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <a title="Slavena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3633862-slavena"><img alt="Slavena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407501224p2/3633862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/555271738?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Slavena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Slavena" href="/user/show/3633862-slavena">Slavena</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who likes YA</span></div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Slavena by: </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3633862-slavena?shelf=grim-reaper">grim-reaper</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer555271738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7325942531320195754">When I picked this book up on a recommendation I was not sure I will like it, because it involves elements I am not drawn to in a book: it is YA, which means it is light on the romance and it is about a girl who is in high-school. Those 2 things usually are a no for me, because since I left high-school I do not think I want to revisit all the messed up adolescent drama.<br/><br/>Another drawback was the cover - it looks very amateurish and it looks like a porcelain doll some high school students drew with</span>
  <span id="freeText7325942531320195754" style="display:none">When I picked this book up on a recommendation I was not sure I will like it, because it involves elements I am not drawn to in a book: it is YA, which means it is light on the romance and it is about a girl who is in high-school. Those 2 things usually are a no for me, because since I left high-school I do not think I want to revisit all the messed up adolescent drama.<br /><br />Another drawback was the cover - it looks very amateurish and it looks like a porcelain doll some high school students drew with black on. I am glad to see that book #2 in the series is coming out with more appropriate cover<br /><br />Despite all those things however I am so happy I picked it up. I started reading this book and it was read in one sitting, I was so engulfed in the story I could not stop until it ended, then I was craving for more.<br /><br />Ember is a high school student with a very unusual curse of seeing how people will die when she touches them, so it makes for a very lonely and painful existence, until the night she meets a guy that does not have a death omen when she touches him.<br />The whole story is about angels/grim reapers battle good vs evil and she is in the middle, I don't want to give more spoilers. The romance was very sweet and the characters draw you in and you have to keep reading to discover what happens next.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book for people who like the supernatural and young adult genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7325942531320195754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Michelle Bolanger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20887864-michelle-bolanger"><img alt="Michelle Bolanger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519665699p2/20887864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410767687?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Bolanger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Bolanger" href="/user/show/20887864-michelle-bolanger">Michelle Bolanger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17800114-ember">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410767687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1017946487320878212">I wanted to really like this book because I loved the premise of it.<br/><br/>Right off the bat, I had trouble connecting with Ember's character. Maybe it was the POV the book was written in. I'm not a fan of the tense this was written in.<br/><br/>Quote: <br/>The window is open and a black feather is ruffled on my bed. I pick it up and my gaze lands on the wall, where the ink of a fresh poem is drying.<br/><br/><br/>What I liked:<br/>I liked Asher and honestly kept reading because I wanted to know for sure who (or what) he really was. I t</span>
  <span id="freeText1017946487320878212" style="display:none">I wanted to really like this book because I loved the premise of it.<br /><br />Right off the bat, I had trouble connecting with Ember's character. Maybe it was the POV the book was written in. I'm not a fan of the tense this was written in.<br /><br />Quote: <br />The window is open and a black feather is ruffled on my bed. I pick it up and my gaze lands on the wall, where the ink of a fresh poem is drying.<br /><br /><br />What I liked:<br />I liked Asher and honestly kept reading because I wanted to know for sure who (or what) he really was. I truly enjoyed the story line, and the connection between Ember and Asher was perfectly written. The poetry flows well with the story and nicely adds foreshadowing.<br /><br />What I didn't like:<br />Raven confused the daylights out of me, and why Ember kept her around as a friend I don't understand. I also got lost because many of the terms used were so similar it was hard to keep them straight.<br /><br />The version I read was the YA version and had plenty of heat between the characters to satisfy me without crossing any boundaries. Will I read the next book? Maybe.</span>

<div id="review_374708629" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/374708629" />
    <a title="Brooke (The Cover Contessa)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7295635-brooke-the-cover-contessa"><img alt="Brooke (The Cover Contessa)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602535404p2/7295635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/374708629?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke (The Cover Contessa)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke (The Cover Contessa)" href="/user/show/7295635-brooke-the-cover-contessa">Brooke (The Cover Contessa)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7295635-brooke-the-cover-contessa?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer374708629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15629501540792947334">I received an ARC ecopy of this book for participating in the blog tour this month. I will give an honest review which is in now way influenced by receiving a free copy of this book. I want to than Jessica and SupaGurl Tours for providing me with a copy.<br/><br/>I will be honest and say that I actually read the blurb for this one when I first added it to my TBR (which was way before I was asked to participate in the blog tour). I rarely read the blurb, but the cover just looked to good to pass up and I n</span>
  <span id="freeText15629501540792947334" style="display:none">I received an ARC ecopy of this book for participating in the blog tour this month. I will give an honest review which is in now way influenced by receiving a free copy of this book. I want to than Jessica and SupaGurl Tours for providing me with a copy.<br /><br />I will be honest and say that I actually read the blurb for this one when I first added it to my TBR (which was way before I was asked to participate in the blog tour). I rarely read the blurb, but the cover just looked to good to pass up and I needed to know if it would be worth the read. It sounded really interesting, right up my ally actually with having loved Shatter Me by Tahereh Mafi and this having a similar theme, so I could not wait to read it once I found out I had a spot on the tour!<br /><br />Blurb from Goodreads:<br />What if you knew when someone was going to die?<br />For seventeen-year-old Ember, life is death. With a simple touch, she knows when someone will die. It’s her curse and the reason she secludes herself from the world. The only person who knows her secret is her best friend Raven. <br />Then she meets Asher Morgan. He’s gorgeous, mysterious, and is the only person Ember can't sense death from. So when he pushes into her life, she doesn’t mind.<br />But when unexplained deaths start to haunt her town, Ember starts questioning why she can’t sense Asher's death and what he may be hiding<br /><br />Let me start by saying that the cover of this book is just totally awesome. It is the perfect picture of how I felt Ember would look! And the color scheme is just beautiful. So who would not be immediately drawn to this book just by looking at the cover?<br /><br />Next I need to discuss the characters.<br />First there's Ember. She is not at all what I would have thought she would be. As a Goth girl, I thought she would be a bit more morbid, a bit more depressed, but what do I know of Goth. She actually struck me as a very typical teenage girl who just liked to dress a bit funky. She's a longer for sure, although she does have one good friend who has seemed to stand by her side. Since she's "cursed" with "experiencing" anyone's death who touches her, it makes sense that she is a bit withdrawn from others and likes to kind of keep to herself. At the same time, she's this beautiful creature, who doesn't have a clue that she's pretty or that she might attract the attention of others for more reasons than her just being a little out of the ordinary. I love that Ember is strong and able to take care of herself, and her family when needed.<br />Next there's Raven, I don't get much from her. To me she certainly seems a bit self-centered, but you can see that she does care for Ember in her own way. Besides trying to figure out how she looks in my mind, I felt she was actually a bit flat. But I also realize that she's not a huge part of the story, so the focus certainly was not meant to be on her. I did feel like I couldn't trust Raven, like there was something she was holding back throughout the entire story. She even kind of mentions it at one point, but she never lets Ember know exactly what it is.<br />Then we meet Asher. Not your typical "hunky" teenage YA guy for sure. He's also this Goth kind of guy, with piercings and tattoos, dark hair and clothing to match. not normally my type of attraction, and yet I felt my self completely and totally pulled to him. He's very mysterious, keeping secrets from Ember and telling her that in time she will get to know him, when she's ready for that information. And the fact that he and Ember can touch makes their relationship that much more tantalizing as she finally gets to fell what it's like to not have someone's death omen thrown in her face every time she touches them.<br />And all of a sudden there is a love triangle thrown in in the form of Cameron. He's totally not Ember's type: blond, tanned, handsome, cocky, dresses like he's walked out of GQ magazine. And she certainly doesn't think he would be attracted to her, yet he is. But, like Asher, he exudes this mysteriousness that has her confused. And, lo and behold, like Asher, Cameron can also touch Ember, although we don't find this out until later as he seems to specifically avoid touching her directly for a long while. <br />The supporting characters give us a look into Ember's life, which is by no means perfect. Actually, it's so far from perfect you certainly feel total empathy for her and her "curse."<br /><br />The storyline is like nothing I have ever read. Sure, you feel that there will be some kind of paranormal element, seeing as Ember sees death omens from people. But I certainly did not expect it to take the turn it took. I thought for sure anyone she would meet would just have the same power as her, more like Xmen than creatures you only read about in books. But it didn't take that turn, it took a turn to angels and grim reapers and things that I have not read about before. It has such a great creaptastic appeal, I was captivated.<br /><br />Jessica's writing is outstanding. It flows so easily, without breaking anywhere at all. Each chapters seamlessly fits with the next, keeping you wanting more. I had a hard time finding a place to stop as I really did want to know what was going to happen next! Probably the reason it took me only one day to read it! Sorensen adequately lays out the dark life that is Ember's with her use of poetry and art. Her writing is gripping and fast paced, keeping you on the edge of your seat for sure.<br /><br />I am excited this is series. The ending left things open, but wasn't enough of a cliffhanger to annoy me. I am really looking forward to reading what comes next for Ember.<br /><br />5 out of 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15629501540792947334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1785411299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1785411299" />
    <a title="Charisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18327958-charisse"><img alt="Charisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543622649p2/18327958.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1785411299?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charisse" href="/user/show/18327958-charisse">Charisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781484020166" href="/book/show/17727238-ember-x">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785411299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7177435253510088120">Ah, what can I say about Ember X. <br/><br/>Well, for starters, it was bloody amazing; even though technically this is my second time to read the first book in the death collectors series. I'm not usually a "re-reader" because there are so many different books out there yet to be discovered, but I needed to read book two and three finally, and since I was buddy reading this with a friend and she had not read book one, I choose to give the adult version a go. <br/><br/>Let me start by saying I equally love "Ember" t</span>
  <span id="freeText7177435253510088120" style="display:none">Ah, what can I say about Ember X. <br /><br />Well, for starters, it was bloody amazing; even though technically this is my second time to read the first book in the death collectors series. I'm not usually a "re-reader" because there are so many different books out there yet to be discovered, but I needed to read book two and three finally, and since I was buddy reading this with a friend and she had not read book one, I choose to give the adult version a go. <br /><br />Let me start by saying I equally love "Ember" the YA version, as this version (Ember X) was not out when I stumbled upon Jessica Sorensen's books with "The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden", but holy hotness batman was this book so much better than the YA version. It had the juice that we all secretly wanted to come of Ember and Asher in the YA version -- at least to me. To my memory, there wasn't a single sexy scene in the other version (but it has been several years between readings, so my memory is a little rusty) Quite honestly, I'm not sure I've ever read this kind of heat in any of Jessica's books, but I tell you, she doesn't disappoint. As she still holds the top spot in "my favorite author" category, I've read almost all of her older books. (I've fallen far behind to date). But in all of those, at least the paranormal, the single only thing that was missing for me was I wanted more romance between the H/h. (Fallen stars/ souls series--I'm totally reading the adult versions of these next--and then Ember) But this -- Ember X was absolutely and utterly perfect. There wasn't a single thing that I longed for when reading, and even being the second time around, I was completely engrossed. <br /><br />Originally, I remember it being difficult to choose between Cameron and Asher, because they both brought totally different aspects to the table. There's Cameron, the twisted bad boy that we all know and love that is utterly obsessed with her and has been around for the long haul. But then there's Asher, the sexy sweetheart that steals your heart and never gives it back. This time around was quite different however. I was torn with Cameron several times. At first he brought the lighthearted laughter that really makes you love him, but his constant flirting with the well-known Mackenzie Baker drove me mad, and for me, he lost mega points at the Lake scene and the night the cops arrived. (Cameron, you really had it going for you prior to this, even given your background) His powers go far beyond the book and even reach the reader. This, I know to be true, because as I finished this epilogue, reading what he wrote for the second time around, I find myself being torn again. Even in his twisted existence I believe he truly loves her, and that's what makes it hard to hate him. His persistence is what saves him. <br /><br />Asher, my beautiful broken man, comes in with a number one in consistency. You have been a sweetheart throughout, yet totally hot nonetheless, and this is what gives you winning points with me. The ending hurt me as much as it did years ago when I read it, but at least this time I don't have to wait to read book two. Ah, the pull. Which will she choose? I can only guess a certain calmness in nature will be her ending path, but still, it won't be easy, because a certain someone has ways of pulling you to him, even in the middle of a hell storm. <br /><br />This book is a solid 5 star for me. It has originality, it has heat, it has humor, and it has the brokenness that I love so much in my characters. Where will death take them next? I'm about to find out.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_600215893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600215893" />
    <a title="Dragana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5084213-dragana"><img alt="Dragana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516620361p2/5084213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600215893?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dragana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dragana" href="/user/show/5084213-dragana">Dragana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15924677-ember-x">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5084213-dragana?shelf=kindle-freebies">kindle-freebies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600215893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5891326470359329753">Ember X is a new adult version of young adult paranormal novel Ember by Jessica Sorensen. Ember, our narrator, has an unorthodox ability. Whenever she touches or is touched someone, Ember has a death omen: premonition how and when that person is going to die. Tortured by these painful and horrific visions (since in her town obviously no one never dies peacefully or from old age) Ember shuns away from human contact. With dead father, alcoholic mother and crazy-artistic brother, Ember's only confi</span>
  <span id="freeText5891326470359329753" style="display:none">Ember X is a new adult version of young adult paranormal novel Ember by Jessica Sorensen. Ember, our narrator, has an unorthodox ability. Whenever she touches or is touched someone, Ember has a death omen: premonition how and when that person is going to die. Tortured by these painful and horrific visions (since in her town obviously no one never dies peacefully or from old age) Ember shuns away from human contact. With dead father, alcoholic mother and crazy-artistic brother, Ember's only confidant is her best friend who is outgoing, slutty, questionably loyal and party-loving'.<br /><br />To make it a little bit more cliche (like this was not enough) enters a romance part of a story. Of course it's a love triangle and it has something for everyone's taste: one blond and one dark hot guy both new to town and both attracted to our heroine. There will be a lot of smoldering glances and Ember's insides will be <i>'curving and cultivating with so much sweltering heat'</i>. I personally could not feel any heat, but maybe it's better, that thing that happens to her insides does not sound comfortable. But Ember obviously liked it, because she sometimes nearly has an orgasm just from heated glares exchange.<br /><br />Ember was tough heroine to relate to. She was usually mopping around either because of her love dilemma, family problems or because she can not deal with her ability. With constant complains and dramatic self-pity through the whole book, Ember sounded more like a teenager/young adult then like a grown up. Although adding more sexual content pushed Ember X into new adult genre, the psychology of characters needed more change and work too, because some behaviour that can be tolerated for ya book feels out of place and immature in novel targeted for older audience.<br /><br />The one part of Ember X I liked was the (surprise surprise) paranormal part. The lore about angels and grim reapers that Jessica Sorensen made up was interesting and we got introduced to the whole history gradually. Ember X is easy to read because proverbial carrot on a stick, aka new info about something, is always dangling just a little bit out of reach, so you trod along hoping to catch it and finally figure out what is really happening. As always, since this is a series, a some things are left unanswered for the sequel but I think we had good back story for the start.<br /><br />Although I liked the paranormal elements of the story, the characters were too immature and dramatic, so I doubt that I will be continuing Death Collectors series. Fans of ya paranormal books who want to increase the heat to new adult level and who like angels, love triangles and tortured heroines will probably like Ember X by Jessica Sorensen but I recommend that you check an excerpt either via Amazon or some other website before buying. Or grab a Kindle ebook while it is still free. ;)<br /><br /><b>My rating:</b> 2.5 stars<br /><br /><i>This text is also posted on <a href="http://bookwormdream.blogspot.com/2013/05/book-review-ember-x-by-jessica-sorensen.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog Bookworm Dreams</a> in a little bit more styled edition.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5891326470359329753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12417760135259156246" style="display:none">Holy Biscuits and gravy!!!!!! <br /><br />This book was fantastic! I certainly would give it the maximin stars!!!   <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/602107803?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RuthAnn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RuthAnn" href="/user/show/6000017-ruthann">RuthAnn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781484020166" href="/book/show/17727238-ember-x">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000017-ruthann?shelf=time-i-ll-never-get-back">time-i-ll-never-get-back</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000017-ruthann?shelf=adulthood">adulthood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000017-ruthann?shelf=couldn-t-finish">couldn-t-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000017-ruthann?shelf=friggin-ridiculous">friggin-ridiculous</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer602107803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1432189058647657156">I made it about halfway through this thing.<br/><br/>I think where I went wrong here is that I downloaded Ember X, which is the adult version of this story. I think it probably does work as YA, but it was a complete and utter fail as an adult story, and the reason why is the author put absolutely NO EFFORT into making this an adult story. She simply changed a word here, a word there, a few details and then BLAMMO! Adult story.<br/><br/>Did. Not. Work.<br/><br/>Let me give you an example.<br/><br/>When Ember first meets Asher, their in</span>
  <span id="freeText1432189058647657156" style="display:none">I made it about halfway through this thing.<br /><br />I think where I went wrong here is that I downloaded Ember X, which is the adult version of this story. I think it probably does work as YA, but it was a complete and utter fail as an adult story, and the reason why is the author put absolutely NO EFFORT into making this an adult story. She simply changed a word here, a word there, a few details and then BLAMMO! Adult story.<br /><br />Did. Not. Work.<br /><br />Let me give you an example.<br /><br />When Ember first meets Asher, their interaction goes like this:<br /><br />Ember: Did you just move to Hollows Grove? I've never seen you around before.<br /><br />Asher: Monday will be my first day. I just moved here from New York.<br /><br />First day? First day of what? Living in Hollow's Grove? But obviously if he's there with her now, his first day has come and gone. So what? Obviously, in the YA version, Monday will be his first day of school, but as an adult, this interaction makes no sense.<br /><br />Other things that allude to the author putting in no effort: the characters still live at home, they treat college exactly like high school, they go to house parties like high school kids. I mean, it was just really, really poorly done.<br /><br />And the romance! HAH, the romance! It came at completely inappropriate times and again, just made no sense. <br /><br />It would've taken a complete rewrite to make this an adult story and I guess Sorensen was just completely unwilling to put in the time to do that.<br /><br />I would not recommend this version of the story to ANYONE. If you must read this book, read the YA version. If you're looking for a good adult read, stay far, far away.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1432189058647657156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13534188690449416545" style="display:none"><b>WARNING: an annoying amount of use of the word "ridiculous".</b><br /><br />Great concept, awful execution. The result: ridiculous characters, ridiculous plot (with plot holes and all), ridiculous execution of a great concept, ridiculous romance, ridiculous EVERYTHING.<br /><br />This book didn't make me angry and hate it with a fiery passion but it annoyed me. I do have to say that it entertained me with its ridiculousness for a while but there's only so much of it you can laugh about until it annoys you.<br /><br />Ridiculous. The only thing I can say about <i>Ember</i>. I already had things planned I wanted to mention and discuss in my review but I just don't feel like putting effort into writing a coherent review for a book that annoyed me as much as this one did. <br /><br />I'm like the only person in a sea of 4 and 5 star ratings to rate this book 1 star, so there's that. Maybe everything about this book wasn't as <i>ridiculous</i> for other people as it was for me.<br /><br />(After using the word "ridiculous" so many times in this <s>review</s> uncoherent little rambling of mine I feel like I don't know how to write it anymore, ha.)</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421020937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12023837181130161487">I am confused, dumbfounded and breathless. <br/>This was one hell of a story. Creative, dark, emotional. <br/><br/>Ember, a girl that can see people's death by touching them has her life thrown upside down when two boys come into her life, Asher and Cameron. Things get confusing and dangerous as she realizes that things are not what they seem. <br/><br/>This was a gripping tale. Absolutely addictive. There was just no way of knowing what will happen next. Jessica Sorenson kept the suspense level on life-threatening high</span>
  <span id="freeText12023837181130161487" style="display:none">I am confused, dumbfounded and breathless. <br />This was one hell of a story. Creative, dark, emotional. <br /><br />Ember, a girl that can see people's death by touching them has her life thrown upside down when two boys come into her life, Asher and Cameron. Things get confusing and dangerous as she realizes that things are not what they seem. <br /><br />This was a gripping tale. Absolutely addictive. There was just no way of knowing what will happen next. Jessica Sorenson kept the suspense level on life-threatening high throughout the whole book. <br />As I reader I did not know who is good or who is bad, who is hiding what. <br />I did like Ember's character from the beginning, did not like her friend Raven whatsoever, which had proven to be somewhat correct. But with Asher and Cameron, I felt slightly schizophrenic. One moment I was on team Asher, the next moment on team Cameron. <br /><br />I hope there will be another book to find out what team Ember is going to end up on and how. <br /><br /></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17581138196530412272">I was captivated by the dark undercurrent of the book. It literally had me hanging off the edge of my seat (and possibly a little talking...erm...I mean screaming at my Kindle) I'm a HUGE fan of Jessica's other series (Fallen Star, Fallen Souls, Darkness Falls; Let's face it I'm a JESSICA JUNKIE) however, this series takes the cake. (and the ice cream- yeah, it's THAT GOOD) 'Ember' had me so twisted, I couldn't decide who to trust or who the 'bad or good guy' was because well, Asher and Cameron </span>
  <span id="freeText17581138196530412272" style="display:none">I was captivated by the dark undercurrent of the book. It literally had me hanging off the edge of my seat (and possibly a little talking...erm...I mean screaming at my Kindle) I'm a HUGE fan of Jessica's other series (Fallen Star, Fallen Souls, Darkness Falls; Let's face it I'm a JESSICA JUNKIE) however, this series takes the cake. (and the ice cream- yeah, it's THAT GOOD) 'Ember' had me so twisted, I couldn't decide who to trust or who the 'bad or good guy' was because well, Asher and Cameron both were amazing characters, not to mention swoon worthy! This isn't an easy thing to do as I usually can guess what will happen and tend to be right...not this time though. I highly recommend this book!(seriously worth the .99 I paid!) In fact, I plan on reading it again very soon! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8561229833553578244">i didn't expect this to be short >.<<br/>but yeah I LOVE iT<br/>i am So looking forward to the next one .<br/><br/><br/>i love this poem in the book :)<br/><b>
  <i> " The ember dies slowly in a mound of ash .<br/>darkness and mourning, it longs to burn fire . but the <br/>smoke and sorrow let it die .<br/>the need for a spark asserts fiercely. but<br/>a spark won't surrender. So the ember continues<br/>to smother. Into ash,into dust, into nothing.<br/>And that's how it will stay forever. "</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>for me it sounds like a prophecy<br/>directing to ember herself :)<br/></span>
  <span id="freeText8561229833553578244" style="display:none">i didn't expect this to be short &gt;.&lt;<br />but yeah I LOVE iT<br />i am So looking forward to the next one .<br /><br /><br />i love this poem in the book :)<br /><b>
  <i> " The ember dies slowly in a mound of ash .<br />darkness and mourning, it longs to burn fire . but the <br />smoke and sorrow let it die .<br />the need for a spark asserts fiercely. but<br />a spark won't surrender. So the ember continues<br />to smother. Into ash,into dust, into nothing.<br />And that's how it will stay forever. "</i>

<div id="review_419453117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419453117" />
    <a title="Corina " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2919367-corina"><img alt="Corina " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558970436p2/2919367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419453117?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corina " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corina " href="/user/show/2919367-corina">Corina </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2919367-corina?shelf=ya-paranormal-hop">ya-paranormal-hop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419453117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8521798022388160300"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13560376.Ember__Death_Collectors___1_' title='Ember (Death Collectors, #1) by Jessica Sorensen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ember</a><br/><br/>It’s finally happened; prepare yourself for the end of the world… <br/><br/>I’m Team Asher! <br/><br/>
  <br/>
  <a href='http://imgur.com/y4MEB' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img alt='How I Met Your Mother Gif' height='179' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391995ra/754736.gif' width='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
<br/><br/>Can you believe it? Because I can’t. Typically I am totally the bad boy type, but for some reason despite Cameron’s allure I’m madly infatuated with Asher. As per usual I have to open my review whilst declaring my love for my favorite male in the book. It’s just how I do things. <br/><br/><i>Ember</i>, by Jessica Sorensen is amazing. The story revolves around 17-year-old Ember who with a simple touch knows when </span>
  <span id="freeText8521798022388160300" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13560376.Ember__Death_Collectors___1_" title="Ember (Death Collectors, #1) by Jessica Sorensen" rel="nofollow noopener">Ember</a><br><br>It’s finally happened; prepare yourself for the end of the world… <br><br>I’m Team Asher! <br><br>
  <br>
  <a href="http://imgur.com/y4MEB" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img alt="How I Met Your Mother Gif" height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380391995ra/754736.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
<br><br>Can you believe it? Because I can’t. Typically I am totally the bad boy type, but for some reason despite Cameron’s allure I’m madly infatuated with Asher. As per usual I have to open my review whilst declaring my love for my favorite male in the book. It’s just how I do things. <br><br><i>Ember</i>, by Jessica Sorensen is amazing. The story revolves around 17-year-old Ember who with a simple touch knows when someone will die, which is why she’s a loner aside from her best friend Raven. This gift or rather curse has been her burden to bear since she was a child and it’s been slowly eating away at her life ever since. <br><br>Raven, Ember’s best friend is the only person who knows her secret at least that we know of. Ember lives with her depressed older brother and an alcoholic Mother. Her Father isn’t in the picture anymore and while I’d love to tell you why that storyline directly ties in with Ember’s whole crazy death gift, which if I haven’t mentioned before is awesome. <br><br>Technically Ember meet’s cocky, self-assured Cameron first in the cemetery of all places. Most people would think that’s a little creepy, but she feels this instant connection to him and at first I’m totally on board with this. I’m not sure at what point I decided I wasn’t crazy about him, but I think it was fairly soon after Asher came into the story. <br><br>Speaking of Asher, cue Raven dragging Ember to a high school party and her bumping into the most amazing guy ever aka Asher. From the minute they meet Ember knows something is different about him, because unlike everyone else when he touches her, she doesn’t sense his death. <br><br>Sorensen does a great job of showing the reader what’s going on inside Ember’s head and how’s she’s dealing with all the crazy stuff going on in her life. This plot is incredibly original and I love how she takes ideas like grim reapers, angels and kind of comes up with her own breed of bad guys. Actually bad guys isn’t accurate it’s more like this struggle between good and evil, right and wrong. <br><br>I love how detailed things are and the way Sorensen describes what Ember see’s when she touches people. The short, rapid descriptions paint a picture that sends chills up your spine. There are so many twists and turns and while there were hints about who was the bad guy, there were also twists that made me question things. I one point I think I thought everyone was out to get her and they were all working together, I was like oh my god poor Ember! <br><br>But that wasn’t the case, haha. From the second I opened this book I couldn’t put it down. It took me a day and a half to read and I would have been finished sooner if it wasn’t for the fact that I had to sleep. If you like a good paranormal, mystery type romance with a bunch of action and death thrown in, then <i>Ember</i> is the book for you. I would highly recommend it to lovers of young adult paranormal novels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8521798022388160300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5487742784177308864"><i>Finished reading Ember by Jessica Sorensen. Being confused is an understatement</i><br/><br/>I do not dare to rate this one.<br/>I will just say 'I read it'<br/><br/><b>Synopsis from goodreads *not sure if I have the ‘right’ synopsis version?*</b><br/>(New adult paranormal version of my young adult book, Ember (Death Collectors, #1). It contains more violence and more sexual content.) <br/><br/>**Mature Content Advisory** <br/>Recommended for readers 17+ due to sexual situations and language.<br/><br/>For nineteen-year-old Ember, life has always been about dea</span>
  <span id="freeText5487742784177308864" style="display:none"><i>Finished reading Ember by Jessica Sorensen. Being confused is an understatement</i><br><br>I do not dare to rate this one.<br>I will just say 'I read it'<br><br><b>Synopsis from goodreads *not sure if I have the ‘right’ synopsis version?*</b><br>(New adult paranormal version of my young adult book, Ember (Death Collectors, #1). It contains more violence and more sexual content.) <br><br>**Mature Content Advisory** <br>Recommended for readers 17+ due to sexual situations and language.<br><br>For nineteen-year-old Ember, life has always been about death. With a simple touch, she can see when someone will die. It’s her curse and the reason she secludes herself from the world. The only person that knows her secret is her best friend Raven. <br><br>But that changes when she meets Asher Morgan. He’s gorgeous and mysterious and is the only person Ember can't sense death from. The silence he instills in her mind and body allows her to feel things she’s never been able to before, so despite her initial reservations, Ember lets Asher into her life and lets herself to get close to him. But the closer they get, the more Ember realizes that Asher is keeping secrets from her.<br><br>When unexplained deaths begin to surface in her town, Ember questions why she can’t see Asher's death and what it is he’s hiding from her<br><br><br>--<br>Just realized there are two versions of the book…The YA version wherein Ember is 17 years old and a NA version wherein Ember is 19 years old. I think I messed up with the synopsis but I couldn’t find the ‘17 years old version’. I am not sure which version I read but if I remember correctly Ember was 17 in the one I read…which means that I bought the wrong version because I was thinking about reading the NA version, lol. <br><br><b>Anyways, I am confused. My head. My brain. </b><br>OK to be honest I was not really tempted to read Ember… because yes ol’ lame me was scared of the cover. Dude have you seen the cover? It is frigging scary! I hate dolls…with scary make-up.<br><br> <span>[image error]</span><br><br>But then I saw the other cover <br><span>[image error]</span><br>and was getting slightly interested again.<br><br>But well, at the end I am not sure what happened in Ember actually. I don’t remember a thing. Even though it was just a few minutes ago that I finished reading it. I thought I’d love it but I didn’t ‘enjoy’ it at all because half of the time I was asking myself what I was reading. It is a shame… that it eventually did not work out because she really blew my mind away in the coincidence of Callie and Kayden. I shouldn’t compare the two books with each other because they are really different in genre –I know-. The idea of the story and synopsis sounded good, really… though the cover scared me off once or twice… But it did not work for me... because I could hardly find half of the synopsis back in the story (?) but that might be because I just couldn’t focus. Besides that, the characters were just confusing. Glad it was only around 270 pages because it was short enough to finish it in 4 hours.<br><br></span>
